Free Talk

Memories of Dai Liang 92

— Yanzi

The Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu took place in the Yellow Sea. Naval Admiral Ding Ruchang was originally a veteran general of the Huai Army under Li Hongzhang. The navy was not his area of expertise. Li knew this, so he hired the German General Hanneken with a large sum of money to assist him. When the fleet was preparing to set sail, it included over twenty ships such as the Zhenyuan, Dingyuan, Pingyuan, Jiyuan, Weiyuan, Jingyuan, Zhiyuan, Laiyuan, Yangwei, Chaoyong, Jingyuan, Caojiang, Jieshun, Guangyi, and Guangnei. Ding nominally held the title of commander, but all orders were issued by Hanneken alone. Hanneken's assistants were two Germans, one Englishman, and one Italian. They were all famous Western naval artillerymen, and every shot hit the target. None of the Japanese ships escaped being hit by shells. Unfortunately, the Chaoyong, Yangwei, and Zhiyuan of the Qing Navy were too small in tonnage and slow in speed, causing them to be circled out of the formation by the Japanese ships and unable to coordinate. The Japanese ships, smaller than the Dingyuan, Zhenyuan, and Pingyuan, could not get close. They used all their firepower to bombard the smaller ships such as the Zhiyuan, Yangwei, and Chaoyong. After four hours of battle, the Chaoyong was sunk by a shell. The Yangwei caught fire after being hit. The deck of the Zhiyuan was completely destroyed. Commander Deng Shichang planned to use full speed to ram a Japanese ship, but he failed to achieve his goal and sank into the waves. Deng's death was the most heroic. Hanneken raised the flag and fired the cannons, fighting tirelessly. His eardrums were shattered, causing him to lose his hearing. Eight or nine of the Japanese ships were damaged. By dusk, they gathered their fleet and retreated. The Qing Navy also retreated to Liugong Island. Being unable to receive reinforcements, Ding Ruchang committed suicide by hanging himself. Hanneken, who had taken over Ding's authority, surrendered to the Japanese because the ships were damaged and ammunition was exhausted, following Ding's last wishes. However, Hanneken remained unyielding. He negotiated with the Japanese chieftains, stipulating that Qing prisoners of war should not be mistreated and should be sent back to their hometowns. He escorted Ding's coffin back to China, bidding farewell in Shanghai with tears. People at the time praised his righteousness.

Removing the Courtyard Grass: A Miscellany of Idle Talk

Watching the Battle 93

Why did Qiqihar fall? It was because one general fought while the others watched, one province fought while the whole country watched! If we want to save China, we must first save the Three Eastern Provinces; if we want to save the Three Eastern Provinces, we must first save Heilongjiang. We must infuse the total strength of the whole country from a position of watching to the battlefield on the front lines. To hold military power and not save when defeat is imminent is to betray the Republic! If you have a pound of strength or a dollar in your pocket and are unwilling to help Ma Zhanshan defend against the enemy, you cannot be considered Chinese. The survival of a country is not accidental. When there are many people fighting and few people watching, even a small country can survive. When there are many people watching and few people fighting, even a large country can hardly escape destruction. We must use iron and blood to write a new history. If we only want to use our ears and eyes to listen to other people's stories and read other people's records, then we are not making much progress. A few days ago, I wrote a poem about watching the battle. Now I disclose it, wishing to work with the people of the country to eradicate this attitude of watching from the sidelines.

(The younger brother goes into battle, the older brother watches;

The older brother goes into battle, the younger brother watches;

Watching, watching, and watching again;

When will the rivers and mountains return?!)

Li Hongzhang After the Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu 94

— Qing Guan

In the Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu, Ye Zhichao, Wei Rugui, Ding Ruchang, and Zuo Baogui were initially defeated at Yashan and then again at Pyongyang. Some died, some fled, and though they were incapable of handling military affairs, they ultimately led to the loss of troops and the sinking of ships. However, the Qing court repeatedly issued edicts to demote, remove, and arrest them in order to demonstrate rewards and punishments. Only when it was unavoidable did they appoint Vice Minister Zhang Yinhuan and Governor Yue Youlian to negotiate peace. The Japanese refused because they were not plenipotentiaries. Therefore, Li Hongzhang was reappointed as a plenipotentiary minister and ordered to go. He arrived in Maguan and held meetings with the Japanese Prime Minister Ito Hirobumi and Foreign Minister Mutsu Munemitsu at Shunpanro. Hirobumi smiled and said to Li, "[Since our last meeting, ten years have passed, and China has not changed at all, which has led to today's situation.]" Li was greatly ashamed. When the negotiations began, Li requested a ceasefire. Hirobumi demanded Dagu, Tianjin, and Shanhaiguan as collateral. Li protested, but he refused to agree. Suddenly, an assassin named Koyama Toyotaro emerged from the meeting place and shot Li in the left cheek. He was seriously injured. When the shocking news spread, the European and American powers were indignant and expressed their disapproval. Fearing this, the Japanese began to allow a ceasefire. Thus, Li's struggle was commendable, and the protests from the great powers were not entirely unable to weaken the arrogant spirit of that small island nation at the time.

At that time, it was the third month of the twenty-first year of the Guangxu reign (1895). The treaty was concluded, which is known as the Treaty of Shimonoseki. Domestic sentiment was turbulent, and Li was universally denounced for not being able to negotiate effectively. The cession of territory and the payment of indemnities were a disgrace to his mission. Within a month, more than a hundred memorials were submitted, almost making him the target of public criticism. Jiang Governor Liu Kunyi, Liang Governor Wang Wenshao, and Hubei Governor Zhang Zhidong strongly impeached him, requesting that Li be handed over to the Ministry of Justice for punishment to appease the people. The Qing court then clearly explained the reasons for handling the matter and the difficulties faced with Japan, and announced it to the country. Later, Li often said to people, "[I never thought that Xiangtao, as an official until today, still holds the views of a scholar,] causing him to stroke his beard repeatedly. However, Li also once sighed and said, "[I am not to blame for the Jiawu peace negotiations. If the Qingyi Garden had not been changed to the Summer Palace that day, spending 12,000 taels of silver daily, and instead that money had been allocated to the naval budget for the Western Empress's enjoyment, then the ships and artillery of the Beiyang Navy could have surpassed those of the world's powers. How could we have suffered such a defeat?"]" This old man was indeed well-versed in the times and was not willing to betray the country. At that time, he was even posthumously labeled a traitor and condemned by thousands of people, yet he still could not escape such criticism. In the past, Liang Rengong said, "[In the past two hundred years, our country has only had two diplomats named Li,]" (Liang wrote a biography of the two Lis). During the Taiping Rebellion era, there was only Li Xiucheng, and during the Sino-Japanese War, there was only Li Hongzhang. His words were indeed appropriate. Apart from these two men, it would be difficult to find anyone better. Alas, may those who bear the mission and negotiate on the international stage not cause people today to lament the past and future generations to lament the present.

The First Big Deal That Made the Japanese Prosperous 95

— Yu Yi

I happened to flip through an old book and discovered the first big deal that made the Japanese prosperous. This deal involved plundering gold, silver, treasures, silks, and ornaments, totaling eighty large ships.

This occurred during the regency of Empress Jingu, around 201 AD, more than 1,700 years ago. Initially, Emperor Chuai's campaign to suppress the Kumaso (a state in Japan) rebellion failed, and he died.

Empress Jingu then rose to power and assumed the regency. She received two strange omens. One was a vow made while fishing on the Matsuura coast, saying that if a fish could be caught with a grain of rice, then every attack would be invincible. As a result, she actually caught a fish. The other was while washing her hair by the sea, praying that if her hair naturally split into two strands after washing, she would be victorious. As it turned out, her hair did split into two strands. Therefore, without hesitation, she abandoned the Kumaso and built large ships, shouting to her children to all attack Korea together.

At that time, Korea was divided into several states. Silla was located in Busan, closest to Japan. However, the strait separating Korea and Japan at that time was not as close as it is now. The Japanese only knew that the state of Silla was west across the sea, but they did not have a clear understanding of its exact location. Guided by fishing boats and directed by compasses, they first discovered the Flying Island and then saw indistinct mountains. Finally, through their faith, they reached the real state of Silla. The state of Silla at that time had never known that there were people to the east. Suddenly, they saw many large ships and many Japanese, thinking that they must have descended from the sky. They were caught off guard and, like the current policy of non-resistance, offered a white flag, presented treasures, and opened the gates to surrender. They even vowed to be vassals forever, never to rebel, unless the river flowed backward and the stones in the river rose to the sky. They also hung bows and arrows on the surrender building and sent their sons and more than eighty ministers to Japan. As a result, the Japanese not only obtained eighty large ships full of stolen goods but also received annual tributes and annual visits from the King of Silla. The Kumaso rebellion in their own country was suppressed without a campaign. From then on, the Japanese state prospered. It is said that this event was strange, but looking at the Shenyang Incident, it is not strange at all.

A Small Chronicle of World Events 96

— Hai Ke

It has long been possible to take natural-color photographs with color high-speed cameras. However, the procedures are complicated and the costs are too high. Recently, there is some good news: British photographers have made another surprising new invention. People can now take color photos with procedures as simple and costs as low as taking black-and-white photos. The area of this color camera is not much larger than that of an ordinary handheld camera, and its price will not exceed five or six pounds. Each camera has three types of glass slides: red, yellow, and blue. The light in the lens is evenly reflected on each glass slide. Three dry plates are immediately taken, but these are ordinary plates. Even the developing procedure is the same as usual. However, these dry plates are stacked on a specially made photosensitive paper, which contains all the secrets. In just three minutes, a color photo can be printed, and the cost of each sheet of paper is less than three pennies. Each set of dry plates can be used to print countless color photos, and even the developing procedure can be avoided. It is said that this new invention will soon appear on the market.

Re-mentioning National Humiliation Evokes Suzhou Memories 97

— Li Xufan

Our country's greatest pain from Japanese aggression began with the Jiawu War. In addition to ceding Taiwan, destroying the Dagu forts, and paying a military indemnity of 400 million yuan, the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang were designated for the opening of concessions (Suzhou, at the time, was still a provincial capital under Wu County). The Japanese official sent to Suzhou to discuss the land for the concession, whose name I no longer remember, came at the behest of the Japanese government. At the time, Governor Lu Chuanlin was still known for his integrity. He, along with local gentlemen Lu Runxiang and Yu Quyuan, jointly discussed the location. Although Yu was from Deqing, he had lived in Suzhou for a long time and his literary reputation was widespread. He was known as a talented scholar, so he was also among the gentry who were able to participate in foreign affairs. Moreover, many people sought Yu Quyuan's guidance, benefiting from his influence. The Japanese official happened to be one of them. Yu was therefore highly regarded by the authorities. However, his vision was sharp and his character was upright, far from being comparable to the traitors of the time. Lu had joined the Grand Council, but he was on leave at home. He was also known for his integrity. During the discussions, the Japanese had repeatedly invaded our territory since the Tang Dynasty, so there was some dissatisfaction. In the end, a corner of Qingyang land outside Panmen was allocated to them. (At the time, Suzhou only had six gates: Changxu, Pan, Lou, Qi, and Feng). The Japanese, because of Jin Changminhua, initially insisted on surveying land outside Changmen. Yu then quoted a Tang poem, "[Past Changmen, the road to Panmen, a weeping willow, a painted pavilion,]" to prove the history of Qingyang Minhua. He also said that the area was adjacent to the Suzhou customs, a necessary area for navigation between Suzhou and Shanghai, and it would be appropriate to open a commercial port there. The Japanese official was indeed well-versed in Tang poetry and styled himself as elegant, so he signed the contract for the Qingzhi land. However, although the area was opened as a concession, Suzhou capitalists did not invest in building there. The roads built by the Japanese were only for the use of horse-drawn carriages. Later, Lu Runxiang proposed opening a road between Changxu to promote the market. The local people enthusiastically supported it. Within two years, the Qingyang market was not completed, but the connection of Changxu Road recalled the red dust of ten miles. Following that, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway line designated the intersection of Changqi as a station, and the prosperity of Suzhou was concentrated in Jin Chang. From then on, Qingyang became desolate, with bronze camels, thorny bushes, and creeping grass. Whenever it was between spring and summer, only the chaotic calls of birds could be heard. On autumn and winter nights, only fireflies could be seen. The Japanese, seeing that there was no profit to be made, did not invest much. To this day, only one agency is set up there, with a few policemen stationed. Therefore, in the past thirty years, there have been few overseas Chinese residents, and although they have an aggressive ambition, the effect is still equal to zero. Moreover, because it is our inland territory, they cannot legally carry out狡計 as they do in Tianjin and Hankou. Recalling the past and thinking about the present, we must give credit to Yu, Lu, and other wise predecessors.

A True Account of Zhang Xuegu Returning to the Truth 98

— Ma Xiezong

Modern discussions about women who embrace spinsterhood are always met with mixed opinions. Those who criticize them say that they are violating human nature. Those who praise them say that they are female heroes. However, the morals of today's world are declining. Young women call licentiousness freedom and consider promiscuity to be love. Chastity has not been valued for a long time. To find someone who guards their body like jade and is unwavering in their devotion is as rare as a phoenix feather or unicorn horn. Therefore, Zhang Xuegu's character is worthy of emulation.

Xuegu's surname is Zhang, and she is also known as Xuebao. She is from Song Shijiabang, south of Cai Town, in Pudong North. In her youth, she vowed never to marry, guarding her body like jade. Throughout her life, she worshiped Catholicism and was highly respected by those in the faith. She was enthusiastic about charity and generous in giving. She paid particular attention to educational causes. Her niece, Ms. Zhang Qinde, founded the Qinde Girls' School in the west of the city, which has lasted for twenty years. Xuegu provided her with great assistance. Every winter, she would take out her savings to help the poor. Even if she emptied her purse, she would not be stingy. Therefore, the poor and helpless were all grateful for her kindness. She was so happy to do good. Unfortunately, she contracted a minor illness this autumn and passed away. Those who knew her lamented the loss of the elderly woman. She lived to be eighty-one years old, remaining chaste throughout her life, never marrying. She is truly a complete woman. The memorial service for the chaste woman will be held on the fourteenth. Many well-known people from all walks of life have sent tributes. My close friend Mr. Xu Xingchu and I presented a silk banner with the four words "Yaodao Guizhen" (Returning to Truth on the Jade Island). In the educational world, Ms. Jiang Xiutan, Ms. Shen Junfei, Mr. Sun Xiao, Ms. Lu Xiuqing, and Ms. Li Yajie also presented gifts and personally attended the funeral. On that day, in Song Shijiabang, white cars and white horses were at their peak. Dark clouds and rain created a desolate atmosphere. Heaven and earth were filled with sorrow, mourning the sinking of a star in the constellation of Bao Yu. (Moved for disaster relief)

News from the Publishing World: The "Picture Album of a Hundred Beauties in Singing Houses," edited by Shen Biyun and published by the Manli Bookstore, has now been published. It is rich in content, beautifully bound, and clearly printed, with gold-stamped hard covers. The price is four yuan per copy, with a special price of two yuan.

The Country Bumpkin Goes to Shanghai Again (26) 99

— Bao Tianxiao

The country bumpkin remembered buying a gong: It turned out that bandits in the country towns had recently been harassing various places. Large groups of bandits entered places as if they were no man's land, kidnapping people for ransom. They did not treat receiving the God of Wealth and 接觀音 as important. The public security bureau police teams sent from the city were somewhat unfair, insecure, unalert, and unobservant, often extorting them. The country bumpkins had no choice but to prepare some weapons for self-defense, gather some strong men, and resist the bandits when they came. They also knew that the doctrine of non-resistance was the most humiliating thing for mankind. They also had to prepare several very loud gongs. If bandits came, someone would see them and quickly strike the gong. As soon as there was an alarm, the sound of gongs would ring throughout the village, and all the villages would respond. The strong men from each village and town would rise up and resist the bandits. At that time, this country bumpkin was sent to Wang Dongwen's copper shop in Suzhou City to buy gongs. The louder the gong, the better, so that when it was struck, the whole village could hear it.

What is a conch? He had never heard of it before, and there was no dish with that name on the menu. The waiter also couldn't explain it clearly. Moreover, that kind of fresh conch was very expensive. He guessed that this country bumpkin couldn't afford that kind of expensive dish, so he didn't offer that dish anymore. Perhaps he could understand some of the more common dishes. [Char siu? Would you like some?] The waiter thought, this is the most common dish in our Cantonese restaurant. [Is there a "chai shao" here?] The country bumpkin misunderstood again and was very surprised.

He had long heard that there were so-called "chai shao" gangs in Shanghai, who were extraordinarily fierce. When they saw that someone had some money, they would come to "chai" your "shao." Someone said: This group of "chai shao" gangs are hooligans. The two words "chai shao" mean "facility". The country bumpkin had a friend tell him the last time he came to Shanghai: [Shanghai is not easy to handle, there are too many hooligans who specialize in extortion for a living. There are small hooligans and big hooligans, creating such a hooligan world in Shanghai.] The country bumpkin said: [I'm not afraid! They want to extort people, but it's always because that person has some money, so they think about him. I am a country bumpkin, I have nothing, they can't extort anything from me either.]

But that friend still warned him, saying: [Of course! You are not a rich person and do not have the qualifications to be extorted. But there are also many small hooligans in Shanghai. They see that you are a country bumpkin who has just arrived and has a rustic look. They can use even the smallest thing as an excuse to "chai" your "shao". Do you know that in Shanghai, someone will come to "chai shao" if you set up a stall; someone will come to "chai shao" if you buy something cheap: someone will come to "chai shao" if you walk on the road for no reason. These are all small "chai shao", but you still have to be careful.]

The country bumpkin kept this in mind. Today, when he heard the waiter ask him if he wanted "cha shao", he misheard it as "chai shao", so how could he not be alarmed?

Commercial News

Fluctuating Financial and Gold Markets Trend Upward 100

The trend is tortuous, resulting in a good start of nineteen taels. Yesterday's gold price continued to reach a peak, with a complex situation and frequent fluctuations. The total was twenty-five or six taels. In retrospect, it eventually rose by more than twenty taels. Buyers were excited, and there were too many short sellers, so the price rose sharply when they covered their positions. The intentions of the industry were very firm. The initial weakness of the previous market was due to the sudden rise in the pound sterling, but major buyers were very eager to buy, as if the exchange rate was clearly flat but secretly tight, and foreign firms were still actively buying. The price immediately rose by more than ten taels. Later, rumors spread about turmoil in the Japanese cabinet and possible restrictions on cash exports. As a result, sellers in the market suddenly became active, causing the price to fall sharply from 678 taels to 556 taels. Later, the foreign exchange market was extremely tight, and those hedging tried hard to cover their positions. The pound sterling had already narrowed to within nine pence, and the US dollar was trading at 32.5 yuan. Optimism prevailed on the stock exchange, and the market was poised to rise sharply, suddenly reaching the border of 80 taels, marking the new market conditions after entering January.

Frequent fluctuations in the morning. The price opened early and fell by four taels to 654.5 taels. Large deals from the previous Saturday did not decrease as expected but rose by sixteen and three-eighths. The silver price fell by one-eighth, but it was not affected. Then, the price fell from six and a half taels to four taels. Tight Money Drives Flour Market 109

Next Month's Contracts Plunge by a Significant 4.75 Fen

Yesterday's flour market opened in the morning. The markets for various months, due to foreign wheat quotations improving by 2-3-4 jiao, had somewhat stable sentiment. However, due to the urgency of the financial situation, buyers were inevitably greatly affected, so a soft sign had already appeared in the stability. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the near and distant sentiment suddenly saw a great shock. Because large and small factories, due to the turmoil in the north, saw a decrease in actual sales, thus each factory's accumulated flour daily saw increases. A portion of monetary relations, near-term goods continued to be released, causing great market weakness, a united and volatile fall (Tianjin banks did have a purchasing, otherwise the decline would have been uncontrollable). Looking at this kind of scene, it was completely driven by monetary restrictions. If actual sales improve, it should stabilize. As a result, this month's decline was 3.75 fen lower than the previous weekend, October's decline was 4.75 fen, January's decline was 3.75 fen, February's decline was 3 fen, March's decline was 2.25 fen, and April's decline was 2 fen.

Wheat Market Plummets 110

Many Take Profits···This Month's Contracts Fall by 9 Fen

Yesterday's wheat futures market presented a picture of initial calm followed by declines. With foreign wheat quotations slightly improving by 2-3-4 jiao, sentiment was fairly stable. In the afternoon, the panic in the flour market also led to fatigue in some sentiment. Moreover, with this month's contracts about to expire, most bulls had to unwind their positions. In view of the lack of a revival in flour sales, the wheat market's outcome had no hope. Therefore, many sold, and market atmosphere then plummeted. In the flat market, one could still hedge by buying, but now, with monetary tightening and little support, the outcome is still difficult to view favorably. Distant months had a less significant decline because bulls were still willing to defend, As a result, this month's contracts fell by a significant 9 fen compared to the previous weekend, December's contracts fell by 4 fen, and January, February, March, and April contracts each fell by 3 fen.

Milan Dried Cocoon Increasingly Sluggish 113

Factory Sales Stagnant, Inventory Increasingly Thick···Cocoon Prices Decrease, Market Lacks Buyers Milan market, since the new cocoons came onto the market, the European sales of Chinese silk have long shown no improvement. Piece Goods: The Popularity of Domestically Produced Yellow Serge 115

Domestically produced military yellow serge has been selling very well recently. Imported goods have been sold out one after another, and the latter batches had no imports. At the moment, the military and academic circles are adding to their uniforms, and all are specifying domestically produced goods. However, most of the output is from the Zhanghua factory. For orders over 100 yards, a 30% deposit is required. Most orders are made-to-order and currently produced. The factory is not willing to conduct transactions with anything other than cash accounts from foreign firms. Each yard sells for 2 taels and 4 qian. Retail sales at the door are 3 yuan and 6 jiao per yard. However, Dahua's quality is slightly looser, and the selling price is 2 taels and 3 qian, and retail cuts are 3 yuan and 4 jiao.

Shanghai's Overcoat Fabrics Not Heavily Stocked 116

The market for imported woolen fabrics and plush remains stable. Because the weather has not yet turned cold, the movement of overcoat fabrics is sluggish, but those who hold the goods are generally optimistic. If the weather turns cold one day, sales will definitely be smooth. The stocks of various overcoat fabrics at sea are not heavy. Statistics show that each warehouse has less than 200 boxes. When the weather turns cold, local customers will compete to buy, and the market should have the potential to rise. Therefore, at the moment, those with slightly more financial resources are unwilling to sell cheaply. Yesterday, Dehua Li, Lao Gong Mao, Wu Feng, and other top-tier plaid overcoat fabrics all sold for 7 taels and 6 qian and a half, an increase of over 1 qian compared to the previous week. Mid-tier overcoat fabrics alone saw a decline, likely due to differing inventory levels and the sluggishness of demand.

Coal: Over 2,000 Tons of Beipiao Coal Arrive 117

After the Japanese aggression and occupation of the eastern provinces, the North Ning Railway was interrupted, transportation was blocked, and the local source of Beipiao coal fines was cut off. The selling price rose accordingly, with each ton recently requiring 10 taels and 2 qian and a half. A ship carrying a load of Beipiao lump coal suddenly arrived at the Japan-China Port Beipiao Terminal the other day, totaling over 2,000 tons. It is said that this coal was remaining inventory from the Yingkou stack yard, and not directly loaded from the mine. However, lump coal sales are not good here, so the selling price also failed to be favorable. It is rumored that it is currently selling for about 14 taels per ton.

Bankers Association Discussed Public Debt Issue Yesterday 119

Ministry of Finance and Banking Sector Successfully Negotiate Financial Public Debt

The Ministry of Finance previously had a plan to issue 80 million in public debt to consolidate the financial administration for the 20th year, as the financial administration for the 20th year urgently needed consolidation. This proposal had been approved by the Legislative Yuan. The Ministry of Finance had also repeatedly negotiated with the banking sector in this port, requesting allocation or collateral. Subsequently, with the Nanking-Guangdong parties holding peace talks, the peace conference itself had an organization for a unified finance committee, and it was stipulated that the central military and administrative expenses should not exceed 12 million for the entire year. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance's original plan to issue 80 million fundamentally conflicted with this, and it was decided to change the issuance to 12 million, in line with the principles of the unified finance committee's plan. This matter was brought up at the finance committee meeting previously held in Peking and was well understood by all parties. The Ministry of Finance then directly contacted various banks in this city again to negotiate, intending to first provide collateral as before. At the same time, the Guangdong delegation's representatives in Shanghai wrote to the Bankers Association, instructing not to allocate sales, as this would violate the principles of the establishment of the Finance Committee. After receiving the letter, the Bankers Association believed that this matter was of great importance, so it convened a meeting yesterday to discuss it. Over a dozen bank representatives attended, including Zhang Gongquan, Li Fusun, Hu Mengjia, Xu Jiyun, and Wang Boyuan, Lin Kanghou, etc. After a long discussion, it was unanimously agreed that the central government's public debt had not been contacted with the Bankers Association at all. Since the Ministry of Finance had directly negotiated with various banks, the Bankers Association seemed difficult to intervene. Fellow members of the banking sector eagerly awaited the early realization of peace in the country. Therefore, there had been a proposal for a unified finance committee and a decision never again to assist any party by issuing public debt that would fuel civil war. Fellow members of the banking sector decided to adhere to this decision unwaveringly. Therefore, it was decided to reply to the Guangdong representatives based on this view and hope that peaceful unification between Nanking and Guangdong could be achieved as soon as possible so that they could unite against foreign enemies. As for the Ministry of Finance's issuance of this public debt, according to the Huadong News Agency reporter's inquiries in various directions, the total amount of the issuance has indeed been decided at 12 million. The Ministry of Finance has repeatedly worked to smooth things over with the banking sector. However, the designated quota has not yet been decided. Yesterday, Minister of Finance Song Ziwen specifically came to Shanghai from Peking for this matter. It is heard that various banks in this port, considering that the central government's finances are indeed tight, and at a time when the Japanese invaders are increasingly pressing closer, the country's finances must be maintained, have expressed their agreement. In about a day or two, the Ministry of Finance and the various banks should be able to negotiate everything.

Song Ziwen Arrives in Shanghai to Visit Wang 120

Under Orders to Report on the Detailed Process of the 4th Plenary Session of the Kuomintang

Explain that the Finance Committee Still Follows the Resolutions of the Peace Conference

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen arrived in Shanghai from Peking yesterday morning. At about 5:00 PM, accompanied by Jianghai Customs Supervisor Tang Haian, he went to the French Concession's Rue Bourgeat to visit Guangdong representative Wang Jingwei. Mr. Wang and Mr. Song met alone upstairs for about an hour, only leaving at exactly 6:00 PM. Wang sent him to the door. After Song left, Wang told the Xinsheng News Agency reporter that Song had come under orders to report on the detailed process of the 4th Plenary Session held by the Kuomintang and explain the Finance Committee matter. Song stated that the current members of the Finance Committee in Nanking would retain only a small number of personnel in the future and that the organization of the committee would still be based on the resolutions of the Nanking-Guangdong Peace Preparatory Meeting.

Regarding the 4th Plenary Session's decision to order Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-Shek to go north, a Peking representative who came to Shanghai yesterday stated that Chiang Kai-Shek, because the 4th Plenary Session resolved to establish a National Crisis Conference that he himself must participate in, has decided to go north immediately after the conference is established.

Wang Jingwei Speaks with Foreign Correspondents Yesterday 123

Organization of Finance Committee Can Be Amended at Any Time

No Diplomatic Issues After Chiang's Trip to the North

The Situations in the Three Northeastern Provinces and Mongolia Are Different

Yesterday, at 2:00 PM, in response to requests from various foreign correspondents, Wang Jingwei, representing Guangdong, met with reporters from Reuters, the Associated Press, the German Daily, the Shanghai French Paper, the New York Daily, the North-China Daily News, The Times, The London Times, and others at his residence. First, the reporters raised three key points, and Wang answered them one by one. The Q&A is recorded below: (Reporter) Does the newly organized Finance Committee in Nanjing conflict with the principles decided upon during the peace conference? The number of members seems to be greater than what was agreed upon at the conference, and there are quite a few military personnel among the members. What are your thoughts on this? (Wang) The Finance Committee organized in Nanjing does indeed differ from the principles agreed upon at the peace conference. As for the number of people, the number decided upon at the peace conference was originally an assumption. The number needed should be determined by the actual requirements, so there is no fixed standard. According to the current number of members, the government seems to have too much control. However, these issues can be remedied after the unified government is established. If there are any improprieties, they can be amended at any time. (Q) Is Chiang Kai-shek going to Beiping on his trip to the north, and is his mission solely focused on Japan, or are there other issues? Who will be responsible for diplomatic matters after Chiang's trip to the north? (A) Mr. Chiang is going to Beiping on this trip north, not to Luoyang. His mission, in addition to recovering lost territories, also involves reorganizing the military and political defenses in North China. As for the issue of Mr. Chiang leaving Nanjing, it will absolutely not be as you all speculate. Since the Nanjing-Guangdong peace conference, both sides have been in complete agreement on foreign policy, which is the responsibility of the Nanjing government. Therefore, Mr. Chiang's trip to the north will not cause any diplomatic problems at all. Moreover, at this critical time for China, the entire nation is preoccupied with saving the country and has no intention of doing anything else. (Q) The Russian invasion of Outer Mongolia and the Japanese occupation of Manchuria today are both matters of interest. Why is the domestic opposition to Japan so fierce today? (A) The Russian invasion of Outer Mongolia and the current Japanese occupation of the Eastern Provinces are completely different. There are three points to explain this difference: (1) The Outer Mongolia incident occurred when Duan Qirui was in power, and Duan's government was soon overthrown. (2) Outer Mongolia only has Mongolians, but Manchuria has Han, Hui, and other ethnic groups, so the situation is completely different. Moreover, the Outer Mongolia issue was declared in the manifesto of the First National Congress of the Kuomintang in the 13th year of the Republic, stating that China will, in any case, unite the five races in the future. (3) The Russian invasion of Outer Mongolia had limitations and was not like the Japanese invasion and occupation of Manchuria this time, which involved attacking and killing innocent people and even using Puyi to force the extraction of salt revenues, a blatant act of aggression. At this point, the conversation ended.

Xiong Shihui Remains Garrison Commander of Shanghai and Wusong 124

The 78th Division Is Under His Command

Subject to the Command of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Headquarters

According to news from the Shanghai-Wusong Garrison Headquarters yesterday, the headquarters received an order from the central government stating that Xiong Shihui will continue to serve as the garrison commander of Shanghai and Wusong. The 78th Division of the 19th Route Army, under Qu Shounian, stationed in Shanghai and Wusong, will be under the command of the Shanghai-Wusong Garrison Headquarters, which in turn will be under the command of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Headquarters.

The Military-Police-Civilian Office Officially Opened Yesterday 125

The Head of the Design Section is Sun Mou

The temporary joint office of the military, police, and civilians of this city, having found a location at the Huzhou Guild Hall in Zhabei, has completed renovations and officially began operations yesterday, but no ceremony was held. The headquarters of the 2nd Regiment of the Tax Police, which was originally stationed at the guild hall, has moved to the Sun Temple. The details are recorded below:

Beginning of Operations: Yesterday was the official opening date, coinciding with Monday morning at 9:00 AM. The weekly memorial service for the Father of the Nation was held in the assembly hall of the office. All staff members were present and performed the ceremony as usual. The chief director, Wang Tianming, was absent due to official business and was replaced by the deputy director, Wang Zhijing, who presided over the meeting, reporting on the preparations, the importance of the office, and its mission. The meeting adjourned at 10:00 AM.

Plenary Meeting: Yesterday at 10:00 AM, a plenary meeting of all staff members was held in the conference room of the office. After a report by the chief director, Wang Tianming, discussions began on (1) the allocation of duties, (2) design matters, (3) service rules, and (4) financial matters. It was resolved that each section would hire one additional employee to serve as a secretary, etc. (2) Sun Mou of the 6th Squad of the Police Corps of the Municipal Public Security Bureau will serve as the head of the design section. The meeting adjourned at 3:10 PM.

Establishment of an Intelligence Office: North Sichuan Road and other areas are where Japanese ruffians congregate. In order to strengthen defenses, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has established an intelligence office on North Sichuan Road, dispatching senior personnel who are proficient in various languages to work there. Now that the temporary joint office of the military, police, and civilians has officially begun operations, in order to communicate and coordinate, any emergencies will be reported to the office for handling.

Military and Police Defense: The office is defended by duty soldiers and police dispatched by the Garrison Headquarters, the Wusong Fortress Headquarters, the Tax Police Group, the 2nd Regiment, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal Defense Corps. All staff members reside within the office. Any incidents can be reported and verified at any time.

Division of Defense Responsibilities: Rumors are rampant in this city. In order to stabilize public sentiment, the military and police authorities have deployed dense defenses. Recently, the defense of the Zhabei area has been undertaken by the 2nd Regiment of the Tax Police Group. The area from Jiangwan to Wusong is defended by the 1st Regiment of the Tax Police Group. In the South City, the 3rd Regiment of the Tax Police is stationed. In the Longhua area, in addition to the Tax Police, there are two battalions of soldiers from the 5th Division. In total, there are about 10,000 people in the entire city, which is an increase in strength compared to before.

Zhang Fakui Talks About His Route of Departure 127

From Guangxi to Hunan and Hubei to Beiping

Willing to Accompany Chairman Chiang

Since Zhang Fakui expressed his willingness to depart to aid Heilongjiang, all sectors have expressed deep sympathy. Yesterday, Lu Fengshi, editor of the *Tongwen Monthly* jointly published by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Vocational Society, visited Zhang to inquire about his route of departure. The main points of his conversation are recorded below: (Q) By which route will the general depart this time to aid Heilongjiang? (A) Departing from Guangxi, via Hunan and Hubei to Beiping. (Q) Can you tell us the specific methods of assisting Ma Zhanshan? (A) Military matters are constantly changing and difficult to predict with certainty. If the troops can reach Beiping in the near future, they will meet with representatives of Ma Zhanshan near Shanhaiguan to formulate a plan and launch attacks on different routes. In short, I am determined to do my best until I die. (Q) Can the government actually provide assistance? (A) Patriotic actions should be met with a satisfactory response from both governments. However, no reply has been received yet. If it is not adopted, I will consider the situation and depart automatically. (Q) It is heard that Chairman Chiang is going north. Will the general accompany him? (A) I hope that Chairman Chiang can go north, and I would be even more welcome to accompany him. (Q) Have there been prior contacts with the Northeast authorities? Will this not cause other misunderstandings? (A) There has never been any contact. Under patriotic actions, there is no such thing as misunderstanding. (Q) If there is no substantial assistance from the government, where will the military supplies come from? (A) I will not retreat due to any twists and turns and am willing to starve to death in Hunan. The above are the main points of the conversation. The details will be published in the 11th issue of the *Monthly*. The *Monthly* has always been enthusiastic about patriotic movements and has recently offered a large sum of money for articles collecting concrete materials for national salvation.

The National Products Promotion League Sends a Telegram Requesting Armed Recovery of Lost Territories 130

Our country has always been magnanimous, adhering to the policy of non-resistance, seeking assistance from the League of Nations, and hoping for a peaceful resolution based on reason, in order to avoid rupturing the friendly relations between the two countries. However, the violent Japanese have taken advantage of our weakness, taking one step further after another, occupying Shenyang and Jilin, seizing Heilongjiang, and disturbing Tianjin and Beiping. Their ferocity and recklessness are progressing with the times, which is unbearable. The League of Nations is unable to impose sanctions. The only way is for our country to dispatch troops to save itself. It has been resolved by the third session, the sixth plenary committee meeting of the subordinate association, to telegraph the commanders-in-chief urging them to send troops quickly and take back the lost territories by force, which has been recorded. Therefore, we specially follow the resolution and request Your Excellencies to make a resolute decision, select elite troops, and dispatch troops immediately to recover the lost territories in the Northeast by force, in order to save the country from disaster and restrain the violent Japanese. We respectfully lead the national products industry to vow to be your rearguard and eagerly await your orders. The National Products Promotion League Committee, respectfully.

The Japan Problem Research Association - Results of Public Opinion Survey 133

Our city's Japan Problem Research Association, angered by the violent Japanese troops unreasonably dispatched to the Northeast, specifically held an anti-Japanese national salvation public opinion survey to see where the public sentiment lies and to prepare for Japan. Forms were made and distributed to all sectors to be freely filled out. Refuting Japan's Five Basic Principles 134

The Sixth District Party Headquarters Sends a Telegram

The Sixth District Party Headquarters sent a telegram: (Omitted titles) The violent Japanese do not comply with international resolutions to withdraw troops by a deadline, but instead become more intense, disturbing our Tianjin-Qinhuangdao area and capturing our Heilongjiang province. They also released a declaration to whitewash their actions and insist on the so-called five basic principles, hoping to confuse international public opinion and obscure the principle of justice. Our people are filled with indignation. Therefore, we refute each of the principles: The three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang are originally Chinese territory, but they have been invaded and occupied by Japanese troops for two months, galloping thousands of miles, killing our officials and civilians, and confiscating our property. Their aggression is not only a matter of policy and action but also an accomplished fact. Our troops have always asked for justice to be upheld and have not resisted. It is self-evident who is the aggressor. Therefore, the first principle, which states that both sides should eliminate policies and actions of aggression, is incomprehensible. The territory of China must be defended in its entirety by the Chinese people. There is no need for other countries to interfere. Since it is said to respect and integrity, troops should be withdrawn by the deadline. To not withdraw troops and talk of respect and list it as one of the basic principles, is it not a joke? Patriotism is the duty of a citizen. Democratic countries have no reason to interfere with patriotic movements. Moreover, the violent Japanese have provoked the anti-Japanese movement. The responsibility lies entirely with the violent Japanese. Our people have not harmed Japanese residents. What is there to prohibit? How can the violent Japanese use this as a pretext for coercion? Since the Northeast Incident, Chinese authorities have paid special attention to protecting Japanese residents in China, and no unfortunate incidents have occurred. According to international law, foreigners are protected as if they were citizens of the country. There is no reason to impose heavier obligations. The fourth principle of the declaration attempts to impose effective protection. What does effective mean? As for the fifth article on respecting Japan's treaty rights in the three northeastern provinces, treaties that have been legally enacted and signed by both parties of free will should, of course, be respected until they are formally repealed. However, treaties that have been declared repealed, treaties that have not been approved by the National Assembly, and secret treaties privately entered into by local officials have not been recognized by the Chinese people and cannot be considered existing treaties. The truth is clear. The violent Japanese continue to insist on the preposterous and their intention is to lay the foundation for occupying our Northeast and destroying our whole nation. Our compatriots should see through their wickedness, pledge to resist to the death, and never acknowledge these five principles, which are absurd and enough to destroy our country and our race. We send this urgent telegram in hope. The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Sixth District of the Kuomintang of China, respectfully.

No Panic Over Cotton Textile Raw Materials 136

The First Batch of British Yarn Will Arrive in Shanghai Soon

A Total of More Than 360 Pieces

Since the Social Affairs Bureau ordered the purchase of British yarn to replace Japanese yarn, the city's major mercerized cotton mills have been actively ordering large quantities of British yarn from the Manchester area to meet their needs. It is reported that the first batch of more than 360 pieces ordered has already been shipped from Manchester to Shanghai and will arrive soon. The second batch is also being ordered and shipped in succession. It is expected that there will be no panic over cotton textile raw materials in the future.

Preparing to Establish a British Yarn Sales Organization 137

Approved by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau / Instructed by the Ministry of Industry

Since the strict economic severance with Japan and the refusal of the city's mercerized cotton textile industry to import Japanese yarn, the various factories with weak capital have been unable to maintain operations due to the lack of raw materials. They have petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau to quickly set standards for laying off workers and to allow them to close some factories to avoid bankruptcy. The Social Affairs Bureau, believing that this matter has a great impact on the livelihoods of workers, rejected the petition and ordered the industry association to inform all its members that British yarn can be substituted if there is a shortage of raw materials. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau specially convened a meeting of relevant groups to discuss solutions, but no good results were achieved. The cotton mills said that the procedures for ordering British goods are complicated and that they would have to advance several thousand taels of capital, which is difficult for small factories to bear. After the groups gathered for a meeting, there were no effective remedies, so the industry association petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau to quickly establish a British yarn sales organization to facilitate the purchase of goods by the industry, or to allow them to set layoff standards to reduce disputes. It is now learned that the Shanghai Silk and Cotton Textile Industry Association received instruction No. 16922 from the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday: "Received and noted your presentation. It has been reported to the Ministry of Industry for consideration and the necessary approval after convening representatives from relevant agencies and groups to discuss remedial measures. We should wait to receive instructions before we go back and act upon their wishes. This order will be noted."

The Inaugural Meeting of the Founders of the Slurry Yarn Factory Was Held Yesterday 138

The Capital Amount is Temporarily Set at 100,000 National Currency

More Than 69,000 Yuan Has Been Collected

The issue of setting up a pulp yarn factory was proposed and after active solicitation of subscription to share by the local Shanghai Silk and Cotton Textile Association the proposal had been basically prepared. Yesterday afternoon, at 2:00 PM, a meeting was held at the Silk and Cotton Textile Association with a number of founders including Zhu Wenqi, Cui Fuzhuang, Cheng Jintang, Xu Yangnan, and others. In addition to resolving various important issues, seven preparatory committee members were elected to actively carry out everything. The details are recorded below:

Key Issues Resolved 139

(1) The dyeing and weaving associations in Wuxi, Jiangyin, Wujin, and other places wanted to change the cotton yarn factory shares to operate a pulp yarn factory because it did not comply with the principles of the previous resolution, and had written to oppose it. The issue of how to handle was resolved by writing to various local associations to eliminate opinions, unite, and urge them to sign up to subscribe to shares so that the pulp yarn factory can be realized as soon as possible. (2) It was resolved that the pulp yarn factory to be established would be named Wanyuan Dyeing and Weaving Factory, and the capital was temporarily set at 100,000 yuan. (3) The scope of business was resolved, In addition to operating weaving, dyeing, and slurrying yarn, the preparatory committee may expand the scope of business in accordance with the capital, and the method shall be determined separately. (4) The preparatory office will be temporarily set up at the San Yangjing Bridge, Ruilinli, Shanghai Silk and Cotton Textile Association, and Cui Fuzhuang, Zhu Wenqi, Zhang Shusheng, Cheng Jintang, Pan Xuyi, Guan Pingzhi, and Xu Yangnan were elected as seven preparatory committee members.

Share Funds Received 140

The accounting office reported that the share funds have been received as follows: (1) Shanghai: 26,516.5 taels, (2) Hangzhou: 117.5 taels, (3) Suzhou: 1,300 taels, (4) Wuxi: 806 taels, (5) Jiangyin: 4,120 taels, (6) Changshu: 162.5 taels, (7) Changzhou: 8,024 taels (8) Other: 13,361 taels. The above totals to 50,699.5 taels, equivalent to more than 69,400 yuan, still short of 30,000 yuan from the 100,000 share quota, which will be the responsibility of the founders to solicit and pay off within the designated period to facilitate the start of the project.

Municipal Government Arbitration Board Decides on Negotiation Methods for Chinese Workers' Conditions 142

Employees to Elect Representatives Today

Regarding the treatment conditions of all employees of the Shanghai Chinese Bookstore General Factory and Distribution Center, after the failure of mediation by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, arbitration was submitted. The Municipal Government Arbitration Board decided on methods to be followed by both parties in conducting negotiations. The details are recorded as follows:

Arbitration Board Notification 143

The Shanghai Labor-Capital Arbitration Committee notifies both labor and capital: "Regarding the labor dispute over the demands of the Chinese Bookstore Branch Office of the Publishing Industry Workers' Union for improved treatment from the employer, it was previously resolved to investigate the number of union members and non-member employees of the bureau, and then elect representatives in proportion to the number of people to negotiate with the employer first, and then report to the board for approval. After repeated dispatch of personnel by this committee, in conjunction with the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau, an investigation into the number of union members and non-union employees of the bureau, excluding short-term workers and employees on leave, found that there were 581 employees who had joined the union and 326 employees who had not joined the union. A roster is specially copied and issued to notify the union to convene the employees who have joined the union on a specified date to elect representatives and, based on the treatment conditions of the 16th year and the improvements proposed this time, to discuss them impartially to resolve disputes. You are requested to comply with the proper handling and report to this committee for approval. Please note the attached methods for electing representatives: (1) Labor members and non-members shall jointly elect nine representatives to negotiate with the employer on improved treatment conditions, but the method of electing representatives shall be based on the proportion of members to non-members. (2) Employees who are 18 years old or older have the right to elect worker representatives. (3) Employees who are 24 years old or older and have worked continuously in the factory for more than six months have the right to be elected as worker representatives. (4) Probationary employees and employees who joined the bureau after August 7 of this year shall not participate in the election. (5) Workers employed by contractors for contracted work shall not participate in the election. (6) The election shall be conducted by signed ballot, and those with the most votes shall be elected. (Note) The employer shall, in accordance with the provisions of Article 49 of the Factory Law, appoint nine representatives to negotiate with the representatives elected by the labor. When electing worker representatives, the competent authority should be requested to send personnel to supervise. Chairman of the Committee, Sun Baorong."

Elections Begin Today 144

The Publishing Industry Workers' Union has scheduled elections to begin at 2:00 PM today at the Chinese Bookstore General Factory on Jing'an Temple Road and the Distribution Center on Fourth Malu. The number of representatives is six. All employees have been notified yesterday, and the Social Affairs Bureau has been requested to send personnel to attend and guide the election. It is reported that the number of representatives elected by non-union members is three, and the number of company representatives is nine. After the elections, representatives from both labor and capital will conduct negotiations. If there is still no result, the Municipal Government Arbitration Committee will conduct arbitration again according to law.

Datong Bookstore Announces Dismissal of Unreturned Striking Workers 145

Business and Other Branch Offices Petition Yesterday

Unions in Zhabei Issue Declaration

Following the strike by all employees of the Datong Bookstore in this city, the company yesterday announced that it would dismiss all unreturned striking workers and hire new workers to continue working. Representatives from the Business and other four branch offices petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, and unions in the Zhabei District also issued a declaration of support. The details of each are recorded separately below:

Joint Petition 146

Representatives from the Publishing Industry Workers' Union Business Branch, Chinese Branch, Minzhi Publishing Branch, and World Branch Offices, Qian Hongcai, Zhu Gongchui, Zhang Sigeng, Li Dixian, and others, went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau at 10:00 AM yesterday to petition for: (1) The workers of the Datong Bookstore must be allowed to return to work with conditions; (2) It is hoped that efforts will be made to mediate quickly. They were received by Section Chief Zhang Zhenyuan of the bureau.

Company Announcement 147

The Datong Bookstore issued an announcement yesterday stating: "A portion of the bureau's workers went on an illegal strike on the 16th of this month. The Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau jointly issued a proclamation, strictly ordering them to resume work immediately, with a three-day deadline. Those who failed to return within the deadline would be considered voluntarily dismissed, and the bureau would be allowed to recruit new workers to supplement them. The bureau has already published an announcement in the newspaper notifying all striking workers to comply with the orders of the Party and government agencies and return to the bureau for work before November 21. Now that the deadline has passed, although a portion of the striking workers has returned to work, there are still many vacancies. At a time when foreign aggression is increasing daily and the Heilongjiang border has fallen, all of our citizens, as long as they have a breath left, should be inspired to stimulate their conscience and strive to revitalize industry to serve as a backing for the government's foreign policy. However, the striking workers of this bureau dare to disregard laws and regulations and destroy industry, which is truly heartbreaking. In order to comply with government laws and regulations, maintain industry, and unite against foreign aggression, the bureau has dismissed all striking workers who have not returned to work and has begun recruiting new workers in order to continue working. This announcement."

Union Attitude 148

Wang Yongliang, a director of the Publishing Industry Workers' Union, told a reporter from the New Voice News Agency yesterday, "The Datong employees were oppressed and went on strike. In order to settle the matter and appease the people, the union adopted peaceful methods, such as: (1) Recognizing the right of the Publishing Industry Workers' Union to represent all members of the Datong Bookstore and subsidizing the Datong Branch Office's operating expenses with 60 yuan per month; (2) Continuing to negotiate the treatment conditions of Datong employees in good faith immediately; (3) Paying wages as usual during the strike period; (4) Not dismissing workers due to the workers' strike; (5) Permanently guaranteeing workers' jobs. However, because the company refused mediation, the matter has not been resolved. The employees are now insisting on opposition. If the company implements the announced dismissal and hires new workers, the employees will deal with it with a tough attitude and are willing to fight to the end."

Declaration of Support 149

The Shanghai Zhabei District unions, such as the Sixth District Silk Reeling Industry Union, the Fourth District Silk Reeling Industry Union, the Shanghai Military Uniform Industry Workers' Union, the Shanghai Gas Industry Union, the Sixth District Tea Processing Industry Union, the Shanghai Binding Industry Union, the Sixth District Cotton Weaving Industry Union, the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Union, the Sixth District Wood and Water Industry Union, the Sixth District Enamel Industry Union, and the Municipal Leather Industry Union, issued a declaration yesterday in support of the strike by all employees of the Datong Bookstore. The text is omitted for length.

More Local News Moved to the Following Page

Page 15

Local News Two

Communist General Defects and Entire Family Tragically Slaughtered 156

The Origin of the Corpses on Yaozhu Road

Gu Shunzhang Defects to the Central Government

Not Tolerated by the Communist Party

Aitang Village Suffers This Tragedy

A Total of Eleven People Killed

Corpses Also Hidden in Xiude Lane

Since the discovery of a large number of murdered men and women corpses in courtyards No. 33 and 37, Aitang Village, Yaozhu Road, French Concession, the day before yesterday, it has spread throughout Shanghai, all lamenting it as an unprecedented tragic case. However, at that time, there were many rumors, all of which were believed to be that the kidnappers had obtained meat tickets, and because they did not prepare the price for redemption, they suffered the disaster of tearing up the tickets, and the country concealed the corpses and destroyed the traces, and said that recently many kidnappers were arrested in Hankou, confessing the whole story of the case, and then a telegram was sent from Hankou to the French police to ask them to investigate on the spot. At that time, the reporter had very serious doubts about this kind of rumor, and all believed that since it was a tearing up of tickets, where did this large number of meat tickets come from, and how were the kidnappers arrested in Hankou? If it is said that the meat tickets were brought to Shanghai from Hankou, then thousands of miles apart, it takes four or five days by boat, and the military police are densely deployed along the way, even the most foolish bandits would never do this. Moreover, the purpose of the bandit's ticket is nothing more than money, even if it is absolutely impossible, accidental tearing up of tickets, the number will never be in batches, this is the most obvious fact. The reporter suspected at the time that this case might contain political effects and other special circumstances. Until yesterday, when the corpses were dug up and sent for burial, someone went to claim them. All the corpses were family bones and flesh. The cause of the case was that one of the family members of the deceased was an important member of the Communist Party. Later, he regretted it and surrendered to Chairman He Chengjiao of Hubei in Hankou. Finally, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek summoned him to Beijing and gave him an important position to jointly plan the strategy of clearing the Communists. Therefore, he suffered the wrath of the Communists, who came up with this poisonous plan to murder all his family members, even the servants and children, none were spared. It is also very tragic. Now, the details of the process are explored and recorded below:

Heaps of Corpses Rotten and Unbearable The case of the French police receiving a telegram from the Hankou authorities on the 21st, saying that many kidnappers were arrested in Hankou, confessing the truth of the ticket tearing, and burying nine corpses in houses No. 33 and 37, Aitang Village, Yaozhu Road, French Concession in this city, please investigate and so on. The detective chief immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate at the address. They dug up the mud in the patio inside the gate and found wooden boards. Looking at the corpses in the cracks, the corpses were piled up, but they were already rotten and unbearable. For the sake of caution, the police station waited for a report to the court before excavating, etc., which has been recorded in the newspaper. It is now known that this case is definitely not a ticket tearing by kidnappers, but a political nature. One of the cruel means of the Communist Party's killing each other. All the dead were family members of Gu Shunzhang of Wusong. Gu is 27 years old this year and is a promising young man. He used to work in Nanyang Tobacco Company and once went abroad to study in Germany. He was fascinated by the theory of Marxism. After returning to China, he joined the Communist Party and served as a member of the Central Committee of the Communist Party and a member of the Central Political Committee. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, he served as the commander-in-chief of the National Industrial Circles Picket Team and a member of the Municipal Government. He was as famous as the important members of the Communist Party Xiang Zongfa, Li Lisan, and Zhou Enlai, and was known as the Four Great Generals.

Arrested in Hankou and Voluntarily Requested to Be Escorted to Beijing Among these four people, Gu's character was the most fierce. The Party once sent four of them to Shanghai to organize the Communist Party's Red Guards, specializing in all assassination duties. In April of this year, Gu was ordered by the Party to go to Hankou to command Party affairs. Gu left Shanghai with several companions and took a boat to Hankou. Unexpectedly, the opportunity was not secret. Gu and his party had not yet arrived in Hankou and had been detected by the Hankou Headquarters Camp. Personnel were sent to guard the pier. When Gu's boat docked, they were arrested. However, only three people were captured at the time, and one person escaped. Gu was taken into custody. When he was taken to the camp for questioning, Gu suddenly said nothing, only saying that he had to meet Chairman Chiang in Nanjing before he could make a confession. The camp did not ask any further questions and immediately escorted him to Nanjing to meet Commander-in-Chief Chiang.

Visits Chairman Chiang and Vows to Defect After Gu arrived in Beijing and met Chiang, he strongly stated his past mistakes, was willing to repent and reform, and presented the Communist Party's internal organization to Commander-in-Chief Chiang. Fortunately, Chiang was always magnanimous and saw that Gu's attitude was extremely sincere, so he did not blame the past and recruited him to his staff to jointly discuss the plan to suppress the Communists. It is said that Xiang Zhongfa was arrested and executed in Shanghai, which has something to do with Gu. At this time, Gu's family lived at No. 802 Weihaiwei Road in this city and voluntarily went to Hankou. Gu's family in Shanghai was taken care of and protected by his comrade Zhou Enlai. Gu was detained in Beijing, and his comrades in Hankou sent a telegram to Gu's family in Shanghai, saying that Gu had been detained and there would definitely be a risk of confiscation of his home. They were instructed to find a place to move. At that time, Gu's family immediately moved to No. 33 and 37, Aitang Village, Yaozhu Road, French Concession.

Li Longzhang Confesses to the Massacre Later, Zhou Enlai learned that Gu was detained in Beijing, and his defection had not been killed. He went to Gu's wife Zhang to ask, "Your husband has now been arrested. If he defects and is not killed, he will definitely become an official in the future and will definitely leak the Party's secrets. If your husband takes you to Beijing, what will you think in your heart when you see your husband?" Gu's wife replied that she would naturally obey her husband's wishes. Zhou heard Gu's wife's reply and immediately had the heart to kill her. That night, he ordered his comrades to help him kill Gu's entire family and relatives and bury the corpses to destroy the traces. Zhou also fled without a trace. This time, the Hankou authorities arrested Zhou's accomplice Li Longzhang. After repeated severe interrogation, he confessed to killing Gu Shunzhang's entire family and the location of the corpses. According to the confession, the authorities sent a telegram to the French police in this city to investigate, and the case was solved and the corpses were exhumed. Although seven men and women were exhumed yesterday, the original telegram said that there were nine corpses, so they are still being exhumed.

More Corpses Hidden in Xiude Lane 157

According to the confession of the captured accomplice Li Longzhang, the number of people killed at that time was as many as eleven. It is said that Si Li, the commander of the Second Division of the 26th Army, and his younger brother Si Li were also among them. In addition to the two stars in Yaozhu Road, four corpses were buried at the same time in the house No. 6, Xiude Lane, Jiaozhou Road, Public Concession. The competent police station has been notified to excavate, but it is not known for sure. As for the seven corpses that have been exhumed, they are Gu Weizhen (Gu Shunzhang's historical age 31 years old), Wu Kechang and his wife (Gu Shunzhang's sister-in-law's younger brother and sister-in-law), Wu (Gu Shunzhang's sister-in-law), Zhang Aibao (Gu Shunzhang's wife's younger sister), Zhang Atao (Gu Shunzhang's father-in-law, 59 years old), and a pockmarked servant (surname unknown), seven people. There are also Gu's wife Zhang Xinghua (21 years old), Gu's mother-in-law and the Si brothers, four corpses, which have not yet been found. If there are four corpses at No. 6 Xiude Lane, Jiaozhou Road, which the murderer confessed to, if they can be found, the numbers will match.

Exposing the Bogus Donation for Horses 158

Despicable Beyond Redemption

After the Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, Ma Zhanshan, led his subordinates and worked hard to kill the enemy, he was in urgent need of supplies and financial assistance due to the lack of food and salaries. This aroused the enthusiastic response of groups, organizations, and schools in various cities, who raised funds to be remitted to the front line for emergency relief and to increase strength. There was a Ningbo person named Hai Arong who came up with a whimsical idea to collude with his friend Hu Ronggui and others to gather and set off on the streets every day to solicit donations from various shops and residents to rescue the Heilongjiang soldiers' military salaries. After the shops, etc. happily donated, Mei and others gave each a receipt, and many people were deceived. At about 11:00 a.m. yesterday, Mei and others were soliciting this donation in Wang Senji Redwood Workshop, No. 53 Sangyuan Street, outside Xiaonanmen. The owner, a Wenzhou native named Wang Ashou, saw that these people were wearing military uniforms, like soldiers, but he had never heard of people from the military soliciting donations outside. He carefully observed that there were many ambiguities in their words, which was very suspicious. He immediately said to Mei that if this donation was really used to help the Heilongjiang soldiers, he would do his best to donate. Please trouble him to go to the nearby post with him and ask the police for the facts, and then he could succeed. At that time, Hu Ronggui, who was standing next to Mei, heard what Wang said and knew that things were not good, so he immediately ran away. Mei's face turned pale and he was restless. Wang saw this and knew that he was a fraud, so he grabbed him and called the police Kong Xiande, who brought him back to the third section of the first district. The gold director took the case. During the preliminary trial, Mei Arong confessed that he was entrusted by a friend to solicit donations on his behalf, and all the donations were handed over to him, and he only provided him with 40 cents for transportation expenses every day. A symbol of Wang Guanjia, artilleryman of the Second Row, Tenth Company, Third Battalion, Second Brigade, First Division of the National Revolutionary Army Guard Army, was found on Mei's body, which was obviously impersonating a soldier to take the opportunity to extort money, which was extremely illegal. He was ordered to be detained for verification.

Tobacco and Matches Industry Advocates for China-Made Matches 166

Letter Urges Improvement of Products to Combat Anti-Foreign Goods Movement

Yesterday, the Shanghai Tobacco and Matches Industry Association sent a letter to the Greater China Match Company, stating: "Dear Sirs, We are writing to you on behalf of our members Yuan Ji, Heng He Tai, Sheng He, Xiang, Shun Feng Zhan, Qian Tai Chang, Qian Tai Xin, Mao He, Chang Xin, and others, who have expressed their concerns. Since the Japanese bandits forcibly occupied Shenyang and Liaoning, behaving barbarically, our countrymen have been unable to endure it any longer. With resolute determination and based on our conscience, we have voluntarily boycotted foreign goods and implemented economic disengagement as an invisible resistance. The establishment of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association prevents unscrupulous merchants from taking advantage of the situation. Our members uphold the long-standing aspiration to promote domestic products as an inherent duty. Matches, in particular, are a daily necessity that has long been dominated by foreign goods, resulting in a significant outflow of money. Since the foreign aggression became urgent, the patriotic spirit of our people has become even stronger, leading to a remarkable increase in the sales of domestic matches. The only regret is that the fundamental supply cannot be fully met, and prices are even raised during times of need. It is important to understand that problems arise when goods are frequently out of stock. Such measures are truly inappropriate. Some foreign goods, affected by the boycott, are trying every means to take advantage of the opportunity, cater to the psychology of the industry, and use various tricks to restore their position. We have heard that several preferential terms have been offered, including: (1) significant price reductions, (2) ample supply of goods, (3) delivery of goods to the stores, (4) credit terms of one month, and (5) exceptional preferential treatment, banquets, and gatherings to foster goodwill. The intention is to entice our colleagues with joy and satisfaction, and to fall for their schemes, disregarding our domestic matches and causing them harm. However, our colleagues adhere to righteousness and will not be tempted by profit, disregarding our domestic matches and causing them harm. However, there are those who may be swayed by their persuasion. At this critical moment, our members are deeply concerned and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we are sending this special letter jointly to detail the above situation and urge your association to promptly forward it to the Greater China Match Company, urging them not to ignore it. In line with the purpose of saving the nation and the public opinion of the industry, we request that you do your best to ensure the supply of goods for export and strive for excellence in manufacturing. This is essential to compete with foreign goods. We also request that you publicize the Greater China's reply to the association in the market to satisfy public expectations. This is of utmost importance." Based on this, we are sending this special letter for your attention, hoping that you will investigate and reply as soon as possible for our disclosure to satisfy the public's expectations. This is our sincere hope."

Overseas Chinese Chen Qinglian from Southeast Asia Returns to China to Investigate Industries 168

Sama Samarinda in the Dutch East Indies is a major port in East Borneo, very close to Mahakam, which produces a large amount of oil. The local products are mainly timber, rattan, bird's nests, and monkey bezoar. Since Mr. Chen Qinglian took over as the principal of the local Chinese school, it has been thriving. Although Southeast Asia has been in a slump in recent years, the school has been able to cope with ease. Mr. Chen, in view of the abundance of virgin forests and timber resources in East Borneo, took a route through Hong Kong to Shanghai in the middle of this month to investigate the demand for timber in Shanghai in preparation for setting up a factory after returning to the south. Someone met Mr. Chen at the Great Eastern Hotel and learned about the recent situation in Southeast Asia and the abundance of timber production in East Borneo in detail. Snow Butterfly's Lawsuit Reopens for Second Trial 169

This Month's 25th Afternoon

In the Second Branch of the High Court Civil Division

The case between female star Hu Die and her former fiancé Lin Xuehuai regarding the termination of their engagement and debt disputes, Hu Die in the first instance requested the termination of the engagement and a total of more than 4,000 yuan in losses and debts. The First Special District ordered Lin Xuehuai to repay more than 1,000 yuan and granted the termination of the engagement. Lin refused to accept this and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court, which has already held a hearing. Because both parties did not appear in court and the evidence still needed to be investigated, the date was changed. Recently, it was heard that the court has clarified whether Hu Die's company's books were burned and whether Lin Xuehuai had 600 yuan in savings at the Hongkou branch of the Shanghai Bank. The hearing is scheduled to continue on the afternoon of the 25th of this month. Hu Die also filed a collateral appeal for the loss of 1,000 yuan. Both parties are expected to appear in court at that time, and there will be another round of eloquent arguments.
