Maritime News Summary 171

Jiang Yu Damaged in Collision The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang Yu vessel, on its trip from Jiujiang to Shanghai, encountered the Dredging Bureau's small boat Li Fu, towing multiple barges, while entering the waterway at Jingqiao. As the two vessels approached, the Jiang Yu sounded its horn, instructing the Li Fu to yield. At that moment, the Jiang Yu had a French warship berthed alongside, leaving no room to maneuver. Consequently, the Li Fu struck the Jiang Yu forcefully, damaging its winch. The Jiang Yu then returned to the Jinliyuan wharf to inspect the damage, make repairs, and file a claim for compensation with the Dredging Bureau.

Gong Ping Needs Repair The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Gong Ping vessel, on its trip to Yingkou to load cargo, moored at the wharf after arriving in Yingkou. Unexpectedly, the Jardine Matheson Company's Hengshan Muller vessel also arrived in Yingkou and, due to negligent navigation, struck the Gong Ping vessel's fore section, breaking the ribs of the forward hold. The Gong Ping has already returned to Shanghai yesterday and will enter the dock for repairs immediately. A claim for compensation has been filed with Jardine Matheson.

Continued Increase in Shallow Draft Fees The water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has recently decreased sharply, making it more difficult for vessels to load and unload cargo. Vessels exceeding 1,000 tons can no longer navigate upstream and must transfer cargo at Hankou. Not only are the procedures numerous, but the loading fees are also increased. Therefore, freight rates must be increased during times of shallow water. This year's shallow water fees were increased by 50% at the beginning of the month. Due to the continued decline of water levels from Hankou to Yichang, making navigation difficult, the six companies decided to add another 20% from today to compensate. When the previous price increase for lumber transported from Shanghai to Hankou, etc., was implemented, it was not included. Now, the six companies have decided that, starting next week, the original price will be increased by about 30%. All customs brokers have been notified to implement this. The detailed list of prices is as follows:

Per 1,000 feet, Zhenjiang, original price 5 taels 5, new price 6 taels 85. Nanjing, original price 7 taels, new price 8 taels 50. Wuhu, original price 8 taels, new price 9 taels. Jiujiang, Hankou, original price 10 taels, new price 13 taels.

Lawsuit for Loss of Virginity 176

Wang Guozhen Could Not Hand Over Feng Qiaoyun

Jia Xiufang Was Taken Back by Her Father for Custody

Jia Xiufang and Feng Qiaoyun, female students of the Shihuaye School in the inner city, went out for a walk in a fit of pique at home. Unexpectedly, they were lured into a hotel in the concession by Wang Guozhen and two other men in Western suits. Later, because the three men could not divide the spoils evenly, a conflict occurred. As a result, only Wang enjoyed it. Two days later, they planned to take the women to Suzhou, but Feng Qiaoyun was handed over to an accomplice and taken away. Wang took Jia by rickshaw south toward the beach, which was not the way to Suzhou. The place was full of pier heads, and they wanted to take her overseas. Unexpectedly, Jia's relatives saw them and forced her to return home. When they were near her home at Sanpailou in the inner city, Wang Guozhen was still chasing behind. Jia's father, Jia Cun, arrested Wang and reported him to the Second Precinct of the First District. Before long, Feng's father, Feng Ziqing, also filed a complaint requesting the return of his daughter. Yesterday morning, the precinct sent them to the local court, where Prosecutor Wu opened a preliminary hearing. According to Jia Xiufang's confession, she was seventeen years old, from Nanjing, and lived at Sanpailou in the inner city. She and Feng Qiaoyun were classmates. The day before yesterday, she went for a walk without anything to do and got lost. Unexpectedly, the defendant, the third person, followed behind and repeatedly called "sister, don't worry, we can take you there quickly." She was then taken to a hotel, where Wang Guozhen raped me six times. Later, he took me out and hired a rickshaw without saying where he was going. Feng Qiaoyun was abandoned. Wang said he would take me to Suzhou, etc. When questioned, Wang Guozhen confessed that he was twenty-one years old, from Suzhou, and admitted the rape without denial. He also said that because he had no wife, he took Jia Xiufang to Suzhou to be his wife. As for Feng Qiaoyun, he did not know how she was lost, and he could not hand her over, asking for leniency. Feng Ziqing and Jia Baocun requested a heavy sentence and to recover Feng Qiaoyun. The official then ordered the defendant to be detained and ordered to bring Feng Qiaoyun to court for verification. Jia Xiufang was taken back by her father for custody.

Reinstatement of the Zhuzhai Town Security Corps 177

The Zhuzhai Town Security Zone in the Pusong District was disbanded this summer due to an incident. Recently, with the Japanese invading and occupying the eastern provinces, the situation has become tense. Moreover, the town borders three districts and is located in a strategic area. With the winter defense approaching and the police force thin, it is necessary to restore the town's security corps. More than 50 shops in the town, including Jiuda, jointly petitioned the Pusong District Corps Headquarters and Management Committee, and it was approved to be restored. The corps headquarters appointed Ling Youjun and Yu Mugeng, two leaders of the business community in the town, to make preparations. The members must be strictly screened, and 38 members were recruited to form a platoon. The preparations have been completed, and a reinstatement ceremony was held the day before yesterday. The meeting began at 11:00 a.m. The ceremony was held as usual. First, Chairman Hou Cheng reported, followed by the preparatory members reporting on the progress of the preparations. Then, Fan Ju, the representative of the Management Committee, began the roll call and continued to speak. Finally, symbols were issued, and the meeting was adjourned.

Postmen's Coats Have Added Numbers 178

In the past, post office coats worn by letter carriers in the city in the winter had been lost. To prevent criminals from picking them up and impersonating letter carriers to carry out illegal activities, affecting the reputation of the post office, the post office will issue a pair of Chinese and Roman numeral copper plates this year to be attached to the left and right shoulders for identification. Anyone without these numbers is not a letter carrier, to avoid public misunderstanding.

Dinner Invitation Turns Into a Bloodshed 179

At Xu Tonghe Paper Store, No. 17 Dajing Road, at 6:30 p.m. yesterday, apprentice Xiao Derong called out to veteran Ge Cai on the upper floor for dinner. Ge did not respond. Xiao cursed downstairs, no different from calling a dead person. Ge Cai heard this and came downstairs to question Xiao. He hit Xiao with a wooden stick. Xiao resisted. Ge threw Xiao down and straddled him, hitting him violently. Unexpectedly, Xiao Derong secretly stabbed Ge Cai under his right rib with a small paper-cutting knife at his side. Ge fell to the ground in extreme pain, bleeding profusely. The store summoned police officer Zhang Xuesi to the scene, who arrested the murderer Xiao Derong and seized the murder weapon. Because Ge Cai was seriously injured, he was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. Xiao Derong confessed to the crime, and he will be sent to the Public Security Bureau for handling.

Thief Electrocuted to Death 180

At 8:30 a.m. yesterday, an unidentified male corpse, about sixteen or seventeen years old, wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, resembling a coolie, was found in the warehouse of the Shanghai Machinery Factory at No. 2877, intersection of Zhoujiazui Road and Gongping Road, Hongkou. The factory used a car to transport it to Tongren Hospital and then to the mortuary for inspection. According to the inspectors, the deceased had no injuries and died of electrocution. Establishment of Industrial Pharmaceutical Company 189

Calcium carbonate, magnesium carbonate, etc., the most important raw materials for China's rubber industry, have always been dependent on imported goods. The total annual import amount, in Shanghai alone, has reached several million yuan. The leakage is not stopped, which is deeply worrying. Chemist Qian Zichao, in view of the importance of this industry and the decline of domestic products, after returning from a trip to the East, traveled extensively to various places in Southeast Asia to research and investigate. Now he has achieved something, and has returned to Shanghai to gather funds of more than 100,000 yuan to organize the Shanghai Industrial Pharmaceutical Company, specializing in the manufacture of these industrial raw materials. It is said that the company is located in Zhenru, and the new factory has been completed. The first batch of goods will be tested by the Dafu Rubber Industry Factory, and it has been proved that the quality is excellent, far better than imported goods. The company's directors Zhu Zhizhong and Jiang Rongmei are very optimistic about the future development, and are determined to increase capital and make greater contributions. In addition to manufacturing calcium carbonate and magnesium carbonate, they will also produce desizing powder and yellow and white dextrin to meet the needs of major dyeing factories. Wang Qiyu, Cui Fuzhuang, Yang Xingdi, and other managers of the Zhentai Yarn Factory and Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory all warmly support it, and the goods will be tested by the factory first after they are shipped.

Weather Report 195

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather in the Yangtze River basin and coastal areas is clear and calm, with fog. The northwest wind along the Shandong coast and the Yellow Sea is increasing. There is a northeast wind in the East China Sea. The weather between Ryukyu and the Ogasawara Islands is extremely bad due to a hurricane passing through and moving northeast, north, or northeast. Its center was within 60 miles of the intersection of 26 degrees north latitude and 132 degrees east longitude at approximately 11:00 AM. A low-pressure system is forming in southwestern China. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this port was a maximum of 70.7 and a minimum of 52.7. On the same day last year, the maximum was 56.7 and the minimum was 46.4.

Acknowledgement: Yesterday, we received the Oriental Magazine, Volume 28, No. 21; the Education Magazine, Volume 23, No. 10; the Student Magazine, Volume 18, No. 10; the Women's Magazine, Volume 17, No. 11; the Children's World, Volume 28, Nos. 17 and 18; and the English Weekly, No. 828, from the Commercial Press. Thank you.

Letter to the Editor 196

To the Editor: On the 6th of this month, your newspaper published a recruitment notice for China Merchants Steam Navigation Co. personnel, which included the statement: "Recently, crew members of the Gongping, Xinfengjiang, Huajiang, and Jingjiang ships, including Zou Weixin, Qian Xiangshan, Cheng Jinsheng, and Yu Gaoming, were dismissed and had their salaries withheld without cause, leading to disturbances at the bureau and various disputes. Li Yunchen has not been to the bureau for four days to handle matters." Our association believes that this matter concerns the reputation of our members, so we conducted a thorough investigation. We learned that Zou Weixin, also known as Zou Liangen, had already been reinstated to his original position on the Jianghua ship during Section Chief Zeng's tenure. Qian Xiangshan, also known as Qian Xiangshan, resigned on his own due to other employment opportunities. Cheng Jinsheng, also known as Cheng Jingchu, had already left his position due to an incident. Yu Gaoming, also known as Yu Gaoming, denied requesting a salary increase and publishing a notice. Ship Affairs Section Chief Li Yunchen, also known as Li Yuncheng, is being treated in the hospital due to overwork and illness and is not absent from the bureau due to this matter. The facts in your newspaper's report are inconsistent with the actual situation. We are deeply concerned that the outside world will not understand the truth, leading to misunderstandings. We are writing to request that your editor make a correction. We would be grateful. Respectfully, the China Marine Engineers' Association, November 23rd.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Ni Baokuan's Message (Opposing Public Sale of Japanese Goods) 197

Since the brutal Japanese invaded our Northeast on September 18, occupying our land and killing our people, in just a few days, more than 2,000 miles of land and more than 20 million people in our Liaoning and Jilin provinces have been completely under the trampling of the brutal Japanese. Our people across the country, filled with righteous indignation, have spontaneously risen up, resolutely boycotting Japanese goods and practicing economic severance, originally as a conscientious action of self-defense to resist the brutal Japanese aggression. However, the brutal Japanese have not awakened themselves. On the one hand, they are advancing troops in northern Manchuria, and after occupying Liaoning and Jilin provinces, they are further seizing Heilongjiang with military force. On the other hand, they are organizing plainclothes teams with extremely cunning means to disrupt our important northern commercial port of Tianjin. This is still something that everyone can see on the surface. Their most malicious plan is to pressure our government in the diplomatic arena to recognize the prohibition of all anti-Japanese speech and behavior, wanting to make our 400 million people not allowed to have a single word or action of resistance, and to be loyal slaves of Japan forever. Under this situation, fortunately, General Ma Zhanshan, chairman of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, is fighting alone, unyielding in the face of setbacks, preserving the personality of our Chinese nation. Regardless of success or failure, it will ultimately be the glory of our Chinese nation's history. At the same time, unfortunately, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has a proposal to publicly sell Japanese goods by the Committee for Economic Severance with Japan. May I ask, the northeastern soldiers, under the leadership of General Ma Zhanshan, are resisting the brutal Japanese invasion on the battlefield with their flesh and blood. However, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the leader of the national chamber of commerce, is advocating the public sale of Japanese goods, disregarding the righteous indignation of the people of the whole country. This must be refuted with condemnation. The only reason that the association advocates the public sale of Japanese goods is to use economic difficulties as an excuse to create alarmist talk. It is said that in Shanghai, there are 11 million yuan worth of Japanese goods stored in the hands of Chinese merchants. If they are not cleared through public sale, there will inevitably be a financial crisis. However, according to the investigation of facts, the maximum value of Japanese goods sealed in the largest stores and all stores on Nanjing Road in Shanghai is only 20 million yuan. Since China and Japan are close in proximity and transportation is convenient, Japanese goods are shipped to China and sold immediately. The estimated value of Japanese goods stored in Shanghai is 20 million yuan, which is enough for one month of sales. The so-called 11 million yuan worth of stored Japanese goods is actually deceiving the people of the country. This must be refuted with condemnation. Furthermore, from an economic perspective, there are sufficient reasons why a public sale cannot be conducted. Currently, the estimated value of Japanese goods sealed in Shanghai is 20 million yuan. This seems to be uneconomical, but in reality, it is not. After the repeated boycotts of Japanese goods are lifted, a large number of Japanese goods will inevitably come in. Therefore, if the Japanese goods are sealed and not sold publicly, the source of imported Japanese goods will stop. Even if unscrupulous merchants want to buy and sell, they will be deterred by social sanctions and will not dare to. If a public sale is implemented, even if the boycott is not lifted, unscrupulous merchants, eager for profit, will seize the opportunity, and some people, seeing the cheap sale of Japanese goods, will exchange money for Japanese goods. Once this trend starts, Japanese goods will come in steadily, and social sanctions will lose their effectiveness. From then on, hundreds of millions of yuan worth of Japanese goods can be sold every year, and the economic loss will be ten or a hundred times more than 20 million yuan. Businesses always have some inventory. Even if Japanese goods are sealed today, non-Japanese goods can still be sold well. After Japanese goods are sealed, the number of non-Japanese goods will inevitably decrease. Therefore, even if businesses have some Japanese goods sealed, there is still no economic problem. If a public sale is implemented, it will be equivalent to continuing to provide financial assistance to the brutal Japanese, which they can use as tools to kill our people. Those who advocate a public purchase either have ulterior motives or are committing suicide. This must be refuted with condemnation. In short, Japanese goods cannot be sold publicly unless a satisfactory resolution is reached in the negotiations between the two countries. This is a principle that our people across the country must adhere to. Any kind of public sale method, no matter how disguised, is giving the Japanese the means to kill us, and is a manifestation of our people's lack of blood, lack of personality, and willingness to be slaves. Alas, General Ma Zhanshan is leading the soldiers of the Northeast with the spirit of fearing no death, sacrificing their lives to continue resisting the brutal Japanese invasion. Those of us across the country who express sympathy for General Ma Zhanshan, can we bear to buy Japanese goods with money at this time? While we still have breath, this ambition must not be relaxed even a little. Our people, let us continue to work hard, and do not let the Japanese mock us for being a five-minute wonder. I hope my words do not come true.

Social News

Is Japan's Population Overcrowded? Wind. 199

By studying the aspect of savings, it is very clearly shown that Japan's population is not overcrowded. Please see the table below:

Year Population Savers Savings

1912 100 100 100

1913 101 105 105

1914 103 108 104

1915 104 108 105

1916 106 116 126

1917 107 129 171

1918 108 147 238

1919 109 168 315

1920 110 184 362

1921 112 201 459

1922 113 212 469

1923 115 226 516

1924 116 294 461

1925 117 236 586

According to the 1912 statistics, Japan's population was 51,753,934, the number of savers was 11,976,223, and the total amount of savings was 192,506,798 yuan. Moreover, (the economic well-being of a country's people and the issue of a country's population being overcrowded or underpopulated are determined by the economic status of the majority of the people. The so-called majority of the people refers to wage earners (including farmers in Japan). If the savings of these people increase day by day, then their economic status is also improving. This is an undeniable fact). Judging from the savings table above, these statistics are very noteworthy, because the table shows the rise and fall of Japanese commerce, which in reality has little impact on the economic status of wage earners).

However, whether we examine it from a geographical or productive perspective, we cannot find any arguments for (Japan's population being overcrowded). Even if we ask the Japanese, they do not understand where the evidence is. Not only can they not say it or produce it, but they may only be able to put on a barbaric face and shout loudly, insisting on the old saying that (Japan's population is overcrowded). But from an objective standpoint, we can only acknowledge that Japan's population growth rate is very fast (but the increase in economic well-being that accompanies it is even faster). Are the Japanese full? The Japanese want to learn from Germany between 1875 and 1914.

Yulian Film Company declared that the company has always been enthusiastic about public welfare. Since the Northeast Incident occurred, it has not only assisted the volunteer army with funds but also donated a large amount of money to support Ma Zhanshan. Now, the company's recently produced revolutionary epic film (Maritime Heroes) has been completed. The plot of the film is tense and stimulating. It will be screened publicly at the Central Grand Theater on Sixth Avenue starting on the 23rd to stimulate public morale to resist the brutal Japanese. Its contribution to the country and society is not insignificant.

Social News Submission Guidelines 201

(1) Text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas.

(2) Limited to news about hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life, and lyrical paintings in various aspects of social life.

(3) Photographs should be qualified as timely, scenic, animal and plant, human, and journalistic photography. Photographs of timely scenery with ladies are especially welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, do not write in sloppy characters, and minimize the use of Western languages. If it is absolutely necessary to use original text, it must be attached to the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for drawing and do not use colored paper. Black paper should be used for black drawing.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript should be sent to the Social News Editorial Department.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If it is necessary to return it, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage stamps should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for text is of three types, three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The remuneration for specially drawn photos is divided into this kind, and the remuneration is calculated separately as in the same example.

Youth Garden

Donation on the Road 202

— Chuan

On the 19th and 20th of November, the Shanghai University Students Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association decided to hold a donation drive from all walks of life to aid the brave soldiers of Heilongjiang Province. At eight o'clock in the morning on the 19th, we gathered in the school, forming small teams of six people from each dormitory room, and groups of two rooms each, plus two female students. Each team was given a small flag and a donation bamboo tube. All the students were in high spirits and set off at nine o'clock.

The 200,000 troops in the Northeast, due to the order of their superiors (non-resistance), allowed the Japanese army to seize the territories of Liaoning and Jilin provinces without firing a shot. Fortunately, General Ma Zhanshan of Heilongjiang, with the responsibility to defend his territory, refused to sacrifice Heilongjiang under the chaotic order. He gathered the province's forces to defend the homeland, winning six battles out of six, preventing the rampant actions of the wolfish enemy. How should we express our respect for this loyal and courageous general? And how should we assist him? We are passionate young people, and we cannot be like the government, merely issuing a few announcements without providing direct assistance. Therefore, when we set off, the team members disregarded hardship and bravely moved forward, doing their work.

Our team of seven set out from Fahua Township, along Xiahfei Road. We walked and solicited donations from passersby and Chinese shopkeepers. We spoke to them with the utmost sincerity, saying, "We are all Chinese people. Are we willing to be slaves of a conquered nation? Currently, in Heilongjiang, the Chinese and Japanese are in fierce battle, but the isolated army in the frontier is facing the strong and stubborn Japanese forces. This is a crucial moment for the survival of China. Can we bear to not save them? Everyone here is Chinese, all patriotic individuals. So, before our country is conquered, please contribute a little to the effort and provide economic assistance." After speaking, we held out the bamboo tube. Some people, after hearing what we said, bravely stepped forward and put money into the tube. However, some people not only did not donate but also deliberately showed an attitude of gloating, extremely despising us, and even uttering some rude remarks. Of course, we did not want to force anyone to donate, but we were not happy in our hearts. We highly suspected that these people were not Chinese.

We walked to Nanjing Road and went to three large companies to solicit donations from the customers. The results were excellent, because they were able to afford to donate and were in front of many people, making it embarrassing not to donate. Especially the women, without us having to say much, took out their money. In fact, they were not particularly more patriotic than the men, but it was a matter of face, and we collected a lot through this. However, one thing made me extremely heartbroken.

We went to the savings department of Wing On Company to solicit donations. A middle-aged man, about forty years old, was depositing 1,000 silver dollars. We pleaded with him to donate some, but after a long time, he still refused. The staff inside also helped us speak, but he remained unmoved. Finally, he even said, "Just be a slave of a conquered nation, why donate?" We could not believe our ears when we heard these words and asked again, "Is he willing to be a slave of a conquered nation?" "Yes, I would rather be a slave of a conquered nation," he said firmly. At that time, one of our team members angrily rushed over to argue with him and wanted to punch him. We did not want to cause trouble and pulled him back. We admitted that this heartless person was not worth wasting our precious time arguing with. He was only fit to be a slave of a conquered nation, only fit to be driven like a beast by foreigners.

In the afternoon, we returned to school. We were extremely tired after walking all day, and our stomachs were empty. However, our spirits were still excellent, and we felt even more happy in our hearts.

On the 20th, news came that the isolated army in the frontier, facing a strong enemy in front and without reinforcements in the rear, with soldiers hungry and tired and lacking equipment and ammunition, had no choice but to retreat to Keshan Town. Heilongjiang was lost. Our blood vessels burst. The government is to blame for the lack of ammunition and the people must take at least partial responsibility for the lack of food. Therefore, when we set off, we were even more excited and worked even harder. However, today's results were worse, because many people had already donated.

A child, about seven or eight years old, was playing on the street with his younger brother. Seeing us coming, he took the three copper coins he had in his hand and gave them to us. Seeing how poor he was, we said to him, "Good boy, you are truly patriotic. You only have three copper coins, keep them to buy something to eat." He still refused and put them in the bamboo tube. His three copper coins were worth more than the tens of silver dollars of the rich. What China needs are people like this, not those heartless seeds of national subjugation.

When we walked to Sichuan Road, a policeman came over and asked us how much money we had raised. We told him that the donations were not much, and we were not being demanding. We just wanted everyone to do their best, regardless of the amount. He said, "You are truly patriotic, not afraid of hardship, sacrificing your time, and raising donations along the way. As for us, who are only driven by foreigners, it is truly shameful to talk about it. However, I cannot help but do it. There are seven or eight people in my family, all waiting for this bowl of rice from me. If I want to be patriotic, my family will have nothing to eat. How can I do that? I am truly ashamed." When he said this, tears almost flowed out of his eyes. At that time, we also sympathized with him in our hearts. There are also many Chinese people who are unwilling to be slaves of foreigners, but because the problem of livelihood cannot be solved, they have no choice but to do so. We should not scold these people but should think of ways to help them. China is indeed lacking jobs.

We went to many places, and many people warmly helped us and guided us. The conductors on the trams automatically allowed us to ride for free, so the work was relatively fast.

On the road, whenever we met other teams, we would ask each other how the results were and encourage each other and compete with each other. The amount of donations, at least, could indicate the diligence of the work.

Our legs were sore, and we returned to school, then lay on the bed to rest. We were indeed very tired, but thinking of the brave soldiers on the front lines, fighting hand-to-hand with the Japanese army, we could not help but feel excited again.

A Collective Cry! 203

— Ding Xiaoru

It is pitiful that China, with its four thousand years of history, has today fallen into a state of peril. Apart from a handful of cold-blooded creatures, only General Ma Zhanshan leads his brave soldiers in a desperate struggle against the dwarf invaders. Although they have won several victories with hot blood, they are isolated and without support. The Northeastern armies are capable of fighting, but they do not advance to assist. The Southern armies, though developed, may not prevail due to climatic conditions. Now, the generally indignant compatriots gather to donate money to aid General Ma Zhanshan. But having money alone, without strength, is of no avail. Given these various crises, patriotic people cannot but worry that General Ma will be unable to sustain the fight alone. Our school (Southeast Medical College) usually avoids empty high-minded slogans and speeches. Now that national disaster has struck, our school's students, lacking military knowledge, cannot make pointless sacrifices to aid General Ma in killing the enemy. They can only (use what they have learned) organize a medical rescue team to undertake the practical work of rescuing the brave soldiers fighting on the front lines. The motivation for this is not to court social approval through ostentatious displays of patriotism, but merely to fulfill the duty of a citizen. Furthermore, among the more than six hundred students in our school, are these thirty-two rescue team members the only ones willing to do practical work? Because in doing anything, rash action or blind obedience is to be avoided. Careful consideration is necessary, such as whether the team members' medical knowledge is sufficient, whether their physical condition is up to par, and the economic problems. Since this is a matter of personal patriotism, and we are all diligent students, the initial funding was entirely from donations and pawnings from the students. On the one hand, the rescue team was eager to depart, but on the other hand, the rear-area work of the students at school was also important. The hearts of the Chinese people are not dead. People in society have expressed deep sympathy and have generously donated money and medicine. Moreover, female students from Jiaotong University have followed suit by organizing a rescue team to accompany them. Thus, on the nineteenth, the rescue team departed. All the male and female students of the school were dressed in military attire.

Page 22

Bearing the pain of sending off thirty-two beloved rescue team classmates to serve our country, we assembled on the sports field. The rescue team classmates arrived in their gear, and the whole group paid the highest respects. During the farewell procession, apart from the solemn and orderly sound of footsteps, there was no other sound. Walking to the North Railway Station, a distance of twenty li, the female students showed no sign of complaint, for their entire attention was focused on the survival of the nation, and they had lost all sense of awareness. When the train arrived, the rescue team classmates boarded the train, and everyone enthusiastically rushed and stood beside the second train carriage. At that time, there were also volunteer soldiers from Fudan, Jiaotong, and Guanghua Universities, as well as representatives from various commercial and industrial groups, to see them off, shouting anti-Japanese slogans. At the last sentence, ("Long live the Southeast Rescue Team!"), they were already choked with emotion and unable to speak. After classmate Zhang Gan delivered a thank-you speech on behalf of the rescue team, the train was about to depart, and all the classmates rushed to the windows, shaking hands with the rescue team classmates. Both sides felt a nameless sorrow, and before they could even speak, two streams of tears had already filled their eyes. The female students were even more covered in tears, standing there like wooden figures, as if they had lost all sense of awareness. When the whistle sounded and the wheels turned, the farewell classmates suddenly went wild, shouting ("Long live the Southeast Rescue Team!") through their tears. After the train left, one by one, tears flowed like a spring, almost bursting into loud cries. At that time, it was not only because they were reluctant to be separated from the rescue team classmates going to the national crisis but also for the current situation and future of our motherland. Only science can save the nation. We, the students remaining at school in the rear, are all intensifying our military training to strengthen our bodies, striving to learn, and enduring hardship. In addition to schoolwork, we are also doing propaganda work and have already prepared to organize a second team to serve as the support for the first team of classmates.

This morning, in the first class, the medical chemistry teacher reported that Heilongjiang had fallen. The entire class instantly turned pale with sorrow. When the newspapers arrived after class, everyone read the lines ("General Ma Zhanshan fought fiercely for a day and a night, exhausted his ammunition, and retreated with tears in his eyes; Qiqihar is gone!"), and they truly lamented and cried out together. Commander-in-Chief Chiang has only now gone north, and there is no news of Zhang Fakui's army departing. Others are even more irresponsible. Are they just going to watch as the Japanese steal our country's territory and heartlessly allow the isolated and unsupported General Ma Zhanshan to fight alone and be defeated? My beloved compatriots throughout the country, Heilongjiang has been lost, national disaster is imminent, and the nation is doomed. Apart from actively preparing to fight the dwarf invaders to the death, shouldn't we (cry out together) for the war dead fighting valiantly and for our country, with its four thousand years of history, about to perish! Alas!
